<div id="review_489643922" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/489643922" />
    <a title="Lise *friends don&#39;t flag*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8191340-lise-friends-don-t-flag"><img alt="Lise *friends don&#39;t flag*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410910791p2/8191340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/489643922?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lise *friends don&#39;t flag*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lise *friends don&#39;t flag*" href="/user/show/8191340-lise-friends-don-t-flag">Lise *friends don&#39;t flag*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Nook 2940016131375" href="/book/show/16137702-vain">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191340-lise-friends-don-t-flag?shelf=ya-na">ya-na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191340-lise-friends-don-t-flag?shelf=made-me-feel">made-me-feel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191340-lise-friends-don-t-flag?shelf=life-changing">life-changing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer489643922" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8858180389521530231"><i>
  <b>Masego means Blessings</b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402653i/782758._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Very Clever</i> Ms. Fisher Amelie what a way to weave a young adult romance into something real, raw and so awful that many people have never heard of or care to. I hope more authors of young adult/new adult romance will take this model and write more stories with substance. <br/>Ms. Fisher, in my opinion was able to combine the best ingredients of a typical love story and tie in some heavy life issues as well as true worldwide events into something that made me feel and fall de</span>
  <span id="freeText8858180389521530231" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Masego means Blessings</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402653i/782758._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Very Clever</i> Ms. Fisher Amelie what a way to weave a young adult romance into something real, raw and so awful that many people have never heard of or care to. I hope more authors of young adult/new adult romance will take this model and write more stories with substance. <br>Ms. Fisher, in my opinion was able to combine the best ingredients of a typical love story and tie in some heavy life issues as well as true worldwide events into something that made me feel and fall deeply for the characters and their life struggles and incite me to want to take action.<br> <br>The real event I am referring to is what is happening and continues to happen to the people in Uganda. Since 1987 the LRA, a violent religious and military group has abducted and forced over 66,000 children in the country to fight with them. Nearly 90 percent of the region's population has been forced to leave their homes. <br> <br>I will not get on a soapbox and preach about what everyone should be doing about this or why you should care; we all know atrocities against humanity exist world wide, but do we care enough and if so, what, if anything do we do about it?<br><br>Just know that this beautifully written love story has a real message about second chances and even if we are not all broken self-centered physically stunning filthy rich trust-fund babies; we can still make a positive difference in our lives as well as others.<br> <br>This is my New Years Message via the words of Fisher Amelie:<br><br><b>“No one can know sincere happiness without first having known sorrow. One can never appreciate the enormity and rareness of such a fiery bliss without seeing misery, however unfair that may be.”</b><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8858180389521530231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/490680101?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Kyle" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle">Jennifer Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17185516-vain">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9916227-jennifer-kyle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer490680101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8214507992061769118"><b>5 Brilliant Stars...A Must Read!!</b><br/><br/>Vain is a well written young adult romance that not only guides a reader through Sophie Price’s journey of self-discovery but also brings the horror of real issues to light that should warrant our attention and action.<br/><br/>This story displays character development at its finest! Fisher Amelie’s writing brings you along the journey and has you feeling and connecting, laughing and crying right along with the characters. <br/><br/>Sophie Price...Vain, beautiful, spoiled, unhappy, </span>
  <span id="freeText8214507992061769118" style="display:none"><b>5 Brilliant Stars...A Must Read!!</b><br><br>Vain is a well written young adult romance that not only guides a reader through Sophie Price’s journey of self-discovery but also brings the horror of real issues to light that should warrant our attention and action.<br><br>This story displays character development at its finest! Fisher Amelie’s writing brings you along the journey and has you feeling and connecting, laughing and crying right along with the characters. <br><br>Sophie Price...Vain, beautiful, spoiled, unhappy, bitchy, manipulating and smart is the queen of the trust fund babies. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402829i/783275.jpg" width="350" height="375" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <i>"I rule this roost because I'm the most wanted by all the guys, and all the girls want to be my friend because it."</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>"My light gold eyes are the colour of amber and are perfect. My lashes long. I am practically flawless.<br><br>And it pisses me royally when girls try to copy me.<br><br>God!Get a clue nimrods.You'll never look like me!"</i>
</b><br><br>When Sophie finds herself standing before the judge for the second time around she receives her punishment of serving six months in Uganda at an orphanage called Masego her world changes and so does Sophie.<br><br>Masego offers Sophie a world outside of appearances and money. It's a world of orphaned children and the inspiring people who take care of them. Sophie builds relationships, works hard and finds love. <br><br>Ian “Dingane” Aberdeen a teacher and jack of all trades at Masego renders Sophie speechless from their first encounter. (I try to imagine what his accent sounds like...swoon) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402829i/783276._SY540_.jpg" width="375" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The interactions and development of Sophie’s relationships with Ian, Pemmy, Karina, Charles, Mandisa, are heartwarming while they face the realities of life at Masego.<br><br>Sophie and Ian’s attraction grows into respect and love. I swooned at the clearing of the bugs, the shower scene and their first kiss. The love that they found in one another was just beautiful.<br><br><b>
  <i>”Sophie Price, you are the most beautiful girl I’ve ever met,” he stated before turning my direction and staring me dead in the eyes. “You are so gosh damn beautiful in here,” he said, tapping my chest, “that what’s here,” he spoke, running the side of his hand down my face, “is magnified tenfold and that is a sight to behold.”</i>
</b><br><br>This book is so much more than a love story. Vain will have you thinking about who you are and how you can make a difference!</span>

<div id="review_495158738" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/495158738" />
    <a title="Natasha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11797762-natasha"><img alt="Natasha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425584808p2/11797762.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/495158738?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasha" href="/user/show/11797762-natasha">Natasha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17254225-vain">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11797762-natasha?shelf=romance-contemporary">romance-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11797762-natasha?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11797762-natasha?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer495158738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4248599692427130504"><b>This book was a beautiful and awe-inspiring romance - such a breath of fresh air...</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380403495i/785015.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Sophie is the epitome of vain - stinking rich & strikingly beautiful, but she flaunts her beauty and uses it to humiliate, manipulate & seduce everybody to do her bidding. She is the queen bee of her evil hive & sleeps with her friends' boyfriends and expects them to thank her for it. <br/><blockquote>
  <i> “God, you are such a whiny brat. If he was willing to cheat on you so easily, he wasn't worth it. Consider it a favor.” </i>
</blockquote><br/>Get th</span>
  <span id="freeText4248599692427130504" style="display:none"><b>This book was a beautiful and awe-inspiring romance - such a breath of fresh air...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380403495i/785015.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sophie is the epitome of vain - stinking rich &amp; strikingly beautiful, but she flaunts her beauty and uses it to humiliate, manipulate &amp; seduce everybody to do her bidding. She is the queen bee of her evil hive &amp; sleeps with her friends' boyfriends and expects them to thank her for it. <br><blockquote>
  <i> “God, you are such a whiny brat. If he was willing to cheat on you so easily, he wasn't worth it. Consider it a favor.” </i>
</blockquote><br>Get the picture? This girl is just pure evil. I kept imagining Blair Waldorf of Gossip Girls, Season 1.<br><br>We also see a vulnerable side to her - she feels truly alone in the world. She has no friends that really care about her and her family's only contribution to her life is of the monetary type. They only expect her to present the image of a perfect family to the outside world and she gets paid to do this. Apart from these social displays, they don't pay any attention to her.<br><br>After she was charged with possession of cocaine twice, she gets sentenced to work at a Ugandan orphanage, Masego, for 6 months. Best sentence ever, mr Judge :) <br><blockquote>
  <i> “You need to change and soon, or you will be beyond salvaging.” </i>
</blockquote><br><b>This is where the real story began for me...</b><br><br>When she arrives in Africa, she looks around for Dingane, whom she was told would take her to Masego. She expects some native African (with a name like that who can blame her), but she is totally shocked when Dingane (real name, Ian) is actually a smoking hot 20-year old white dude. Her typical charms doesn't have any affect on him and he treats her with disdain, because he sees her for the vain, spoiled brat that she is.<br><br>It was a massive shock for Sophie when they arrived at the orphanage. My heart also broke.<br><blockquote>
  <i>"That’s when I saw them, noticed what Dingane was trying to prepare me for. Children, all ages, missing arms, eyes, parts of their faces, even legs. I held back my gasp and met Dingane’s eyes. They were warm and full of understanding but for the children only. He looked at me sternly and his eyes conveyed what he wanted me to do.<br>I looked down on them, half-smiling, trying so very hard to look sincere when all I wanted to do was run and lock myself away from their terribly shocking faces. I had never in my life thought humans could endure such physical damage and survive." </i>
</blockquote><br>Life at the orgaphanage is really hard... this is not luxury camping. They are surviving on only the minimal necessities. But the kids are all happy and smiling - they are alive and they are grateful for that.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380403495i/785016._SX540_.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Their innocence is addicting, their hope is catching and I'm happy to be surrounded by them.” <i></i></i>
</blockquote><br>Sophie is teamed up with Ian to teach the kids, but the relationship between them feels extremely strained.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“You won’t last out here. You’ll stay blind to the environment that surrounds you. You’ll live in your clean, perfect bubble and return to your posh life come six months. You are....you. I know your kind. I’ve seen it all before. You will never wake up. Not really,” <i></i></i>
</blockquote><br>They spent a lot of time together performing their duties and survived some terrifying things - diseases, attacks around camp, etc - the type of things that change people. Sophie didn't fight it, she acted selfless and underwent an amazing transformation. She even developed a special bond with a little girl.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380403495i/785017.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And then the part that all of us has been waiting for...</b><br><br>She realizes that Ian doesn't hate her and that they are actually kindred spirits.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“I’m just-I was quick to judge. I was wrong when I thought you couldn’t change. So few can do it.”<br>“You think I’ve changed?”<br>“Soph,” he said quietly, reaching for me, but I refused to budge. “You’ve been transformed for a while.”</i>
  <br>
</blockquote><br><br>A beautiful friendship starts to blossom between them and they fall for each other, hard! <br><blockquote>
  <i>“You have no idea what you do to me. I've felt things for you these past few months that don't seem healthy. I've wanted you so desperately I'm afraid it may not be natural. You consume my thoughts, Sophie...You've arrested my senses and I can't seem to get enough of you. That's what scares me. I'm so deep there's no getting out for me. You own me, you know?” </i>
  <br>
</blockquote><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>But relationships in Masego are not easy, there are so much more important issues that demands their time and attention. Another burning issue between them is what will happen when Sophie's 6 month sentence is over? Will she remain in Masego or return to her old life?<br><br>I don't want to give away the ending, so I think I'll stop while I am ahead here. The most important question... do we get a HEA? Oh hell yes!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4248599692427130504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_754088378" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754088378" />
    <a title="La-Lionne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11644154-la-lionne"><img alt="La-Lionne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458815714p2/11644154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/754088378?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="La-Lionne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="La-Lionne" href="/user/show/11644154-la-lionne">La-Lionne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18331807-vain">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=frustrating">frustrating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=dumb-heroine">dumb-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=badly-written">badly-written</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=just-blah">just-blah</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=could-not-finish">could-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=reviews-say-yay-i-say-nay">reviews-say-yay-i-say-nay</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer754088378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2642180743507085227"><b>***1.5 decieving stars***</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389522099ra/8037996.gif' width='300' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>If you’re looking for a story about a good, humble girl, who’s been hurt by someone she thought she could trust, only to find out she’s not as vulnerable as she thought she was and discovers an empowering side of herself that falls in love with the guy who helps her find that self, blah, blah, blah...then you’re gonna’ hate my story.</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>LIE! LIE! LIE! This is exactly what this story is about and how heroine is. She's angry, bitter, whoring around coldhearted bitch, who d</span>
  <span id="freeText2642180743507085227" style="display:none"><b>***1.5 decieving stars***</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389522099ra/8037996.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>
  <blockquote>If you’re looking for a story about a good, humble girl, who’s been hurt by someone she thought she could trust, only to find out she’s not as vulnerable as she thought she was and discovers an empowering side of herself that falls in love with the guy who helps her find that self, blah, blah, blah...then you’re gonna’ hate my story.</blockquote>
</i><br><br>LIE! LIE! LIE! This is exactly what this story is about and how heroine is. She's angry, bitter, whoring around coldhearted bitch, who doesn't have any regards for other people's feelings, because she didn't get the attention she wanted from her parents.<br>And I fell for it! The way this book is described in the blurb made me think that this story will be different. I've read tons of reviews, where words 'unique', 'different' and 'not your typical' were used. Now, I sit here and wonder what book are all those people describing? Obviously not this one, because there is absolutely nothing unique or different about this book. This book is just another YA sob-fest.<br><br>When I read the first chapter I got really exited, because I thought I'm going to like her bitchy personality. At that time, it did feel different. She felt cold and detached. I couldn't relate to her as a person, but I was enjoying reading about her. Author didn't dwell on heroine's emotions, the writing felt a little robotic, and at first, I thought it was done on purpose, to make our heroine feel more distant. Later it turned out that it wasn't the case, and that it was simply bad writing. <br><br>As a punishment, for constantly getting herself into trouble, this girl gets send to Africa, Uganda, to work in the orphanage. <br>All horros considered, author chose a beautiful place to send her heroine to. But I never got a decent picture of the place, because the descriptions of it were sooo vague. There was a huge baobab tree, bugs in the shower, couple of buildings and kids running around. That's it. I've read better descriptions of Uganda on Wikipedia. Not only that, based on the directions to the orphanage, that author gave me, would place the orphanage in the middle of freaking Lake Victoria. Yes, I googled the map of Uganda, that's how I know. I did it because I needed to get a better picture of the place. I know that it's a fictional story and that the orphanage doesn't exist in real life, but author did use real names of small towns and cities in Uganda, why not place the imaginary orphanage on a dry land??? Google maps showed that there are plenty of it!!!<br><br>Another problem I had was the emotional side of two main characters. This is the note I had in the book about halfway through: <i>Author doesn't portray emotions very well, and her descriptions of important situations are lacking.</i> I like when authors leave some things to my imagination, but there were too many blanks to fill in. <br>Seing all those suffering children was a turning point for our heroine. It made her realize how precious life is and how good she had back home. But she came to that realization way too quickly. One day she just simply understood everything. Author didn't bother telling me how she came to that conclusion. It felt like "Duh, those kids are parentless, I don't need to explain to you how much their lives suck, do I?" <br>There was a scene where kids got really scared, but no one at the camp tried to comfort them or reassure that everything will be alright. That pissed me off.<br><br>This story is not about helping kids, I get it, it's a story about a girl falling in love with a guy. But still, I would have loved to see our heroine doing something else other than drooling over a hot guy. At that moment I realized that this story is no different from many other YA stories I've read. You could say that she fell in love with him because he was working with kids, but that's not true at all. Because if you bothered to pay attention to how many times she described what he was doing, rather then the glances he gave her, or his physical attributes, you would have known that the latter outweighed the former. So, the bottom line is: she fell in love with him not because he was a good Samaritan, but because he was hot.<br><br>As for the guy in question; I don't have much good to say about him either. The fact that he dedicated his life to helping children in need is admirable, I guess that's why I'm giving this book 1.5 stars rather than zero, but he, too, had many flaws that bothered me. At first, when I read that he cleaned the shower for her, I thought it was romantic, but later I realized that he was just as superficial as she was. Why not let her shower in a shower full of bugs? That would teach her a lesson. Wasn't that the whole point, her learning something on this trip? He says "I know your type" meaning she's just another spoiled rich girl, then he goes cleaning the shower before she uses it???? Oh, and another note I made when he said "I know your type.": <i>How did he know her type? Is that orphanage used as an exile for spoiled rich bitches?</i><br><br>Later, I realized that author's knowledge of Uganda was based on... I don't know on what exactly. On thin air I guess. There was zero research done before writing this book. Our heroine was shocked that Ian was white. Really??? It's like author based her knowledge about Africa and Uganda on commercials we see on TV right before Christmas. It's sad, because even with a decent research using google, this story would have been much better. Unfortunately, author didn't bother even with that.<br><br>This story reminded me of a book I've read a while back, where author invented a country Bezakistan. I didn't like the book, but at least I wasn't upset with author for making shit up. It's her made-up country, she can write what ever she wants and create what ever characters she likes. However, with this story, it's a whole another matter. When you choose subjects such as poverty in Africa, LRA, child hunger, life changing experience and love, you better make sure you have your facts straight!<br><br>I dove into it having a very high expectations, because of the blurb and tons of glowing reviews, and was left hugely disappointed. I would never recommend this book to anyone who has at least a little bit of knowledge about Uganda and the issues that country is facing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2642180743507085227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_487181927" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/487181927" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/487181927?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Nook 2940016131375" href="/book/show/16137702-vain">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer487181927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1714950888288684270">Wow! I didn’t have any expectations for this book, I have never read anything by this author... but it blew me away! It was just an amazing story! It had me hooked from the every beginning. You fell in love with the characters, and the writing was just beautiful!<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Vanity’s a debilitating affliction. You’re so absorbed in yourself it’s impossible to love anyone other than oneself, leaving you weak without realization of it. It’s quite sad. You’ve no idea with you’re missing either. You will neve</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText1714950888288684270" style="display:none">Wow! I didn’t have any expectations for this book, I have never read anything by this author... but it blew me away! It was just an amazing story! It had me hooked from the every beginning. You fell in love with the characters, and the writing was just beautiful!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Vanity’s a debilitating affliction. You’re so absorbed in yourself it’s impossible to love anyone other than oneself, leaving you weak without realization of it. It’s quite sad. You’ve no idea with you’re missing either. You will never know real love an your life will pass you by. </i>
</b> <br /><br />Sophie Price fits the title of this book perfectly. She is vain. She is a rich and spoiled girl, and is the queen of the other rich, spoiled and entitled. <br /><b>
  <i>No, I ruled because I was the hottest. You see, I’m one of the beautiful people.</i>
</b><br />She has no true friends, except maybe one (Spencer) and she is so unhappy in her life, she spends her weekends doing drugs, sleeping around with her friends boyfriends and spending her daddy’s money. As long as she keeps up appearances, her parents could care less about what she does or how she acts. <br /><i>
  <b>If I faced what I’d truly created for myself, a life of debauchery and seedy fulfillment, I knew I couldn't have lived another day and self preservation was very much still alive in me. I loved myself too much to say goodbye. So, I would go on living just as I had been because it was the only life I knew.</b>
</i><br /><br />When she gets busted for drugs, the second time, and ruins a business contact for her father, she gets a wake-up call. When she goes to court with her father’s attorney Pemmy, the only adult in her life that actually cares about her, she finds out that instead of jail/rehab/community service, she will be going to Uganda to work at an orphanage for 6 months. Pemmy knows Sophie is better than who she has been and thinks this will be good for her. Loved Pemmy! <br /><b>
  <i>“You need to change and soon, or you will be beyond salvaging.” “Nothing can prevent me from becoming what I already am.” I proclaimed, honest with myself for the very first time. “True, but people can change my dear, and I know you’re capable of being better than this girl you’ve created for yourself.”</i>
</b><br /><br />She spends her last few days at home with her friend Spencer, then heads to Uganda for 6 months that will completely change her life. She meets Ian (dear god, I loved him loved loved loved!) and Charles and Karina, who ran the orphanage. They were such wonderful and selfless people, who embraced Sophie right away. She grew to love the two of them and finally had adults to aspire to be like. <br /><b>
  <i>I decided right then and there that I would be gobbling them up as long as I had the opportunity. I would learn from them. I would study them. I would endeavor to be like them. </i>
</b><br /><br />At first, Sophie was a little taken aback by the children at the orphanage. Most of them had parents who were killed by Kony/LRA and a lot of them were sick or deformed in someway, but she quickly jumped in and started to really teach them and help them, and love them. She worked closley with Ian who she felt iinstantly attracted to. Ian didn’t take Sophie’s crap. I loved that about him! He had a past not so different from Sophie’s in some ways, and he wasn’t afraid to call her out on hers. <br /><b>
  <i>“Bullshit. You don’t really believe that. You want to stick with what’s easy for you. You foresee the amount of work it would take to transform yourself and you’re too frightened to embrace the challenge. Now, that, Sophie Price, is a real weakness.”</i>
</b><br /><br />As time goes by at the orphanage, Sophie really discovers herself. She learns what it means to have true friends, people who love her and count on her, not for how she looks or how much money she has, but who she is as a person. This story is one of self discovery for Sophie. <br /><b>
  <i>I knew then that I never needed to be kept by a man. What I needed was to love myself, to want to keep myself around. And in that revelation, I knew that if I wanted to keep myself, that a man wanting to keep me would just be a by-product. Who wouldn’t want to keep someone who respected himself or herself?<br /><br />I’d come to Uganda to fulfill a mandatory sentence but was being fulfilled in a completely unexpected manner and happily, with my full consent. I’d come to help teach these children but instead they were teaching me. </i>
</b><br /><br />As Sophie and Ian’s relationship grows, things start to change even more for Sophie. Ian was so great, really loved him. He melted my heart! He fell hard for Sophie. <br /><b>
  <i>“You’ve arrested my senses and I can’t seem to get enough of you. That’s what scares me. I’m so deep there’s no getting out for me. You own me, you know?”</i>
</b><br />Sophie ends up meeting Ian’s family, and they love her... except for his mother. Ugh. When they get back from visiting his family, something terrible happens at the orphanage... breaks my heart. Sophie ends up having to go home for court. And you will have to read the book to find out how it ends, don't want to spoil to much!<br /><br /><br />I’m sure this is a lengthy review, but this story really touched me. Not only did it have a beautiful message of self discovery, you really got to see the conditions others live in and reading the story of these African children will make you not take things for granted. Sure it had some love and romance, but it was so much bigger than just that. This is a book I would recommend to everyone!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1714950888288684270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_494808720" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/494808720" />
    <a title="Natasha is a Book Junkie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie"><img alt="Natasha is a Book Junkie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585046882p2/9389992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/494808720?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasha is a Book Junkie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasha is a Book Junkie" href="/user/show/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie">Natasha is a Book Junkie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17254225-vain">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer494808720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5305150356142571413"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“No one can know sincere happiness, Sophie, without first having known sorrow. One can never appreciate the enormity and rareness of such a fiery bliss without seeing misery, however unfair that may be.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>There’s a proverb that says, <i>“Just when the caterpillar thought the world was over, it became a butterfly.”</i> This is the truly beautiful story of a young woman’s journey from egocentricity to self-awareness, from having regard only for herself to being willing to sacrifice her own happ</span>
  <span id="freeText5305150356142571413" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“No one can know sincere happiness, Sophie, without first having known sorrow. One can never appreciate the enormity and rareness of such a fiery bliss without seeing misery, however unfair that may be.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />There’s a proverb that says, <i>“Just when the caterpillar thought the world was over, it became a butterfly.”</i> This is the truly beautiful story of a young woman’s journey from egocentricity to self-awareness, from having regard only for herself to being willing to sacrifice her own happiness for the sake of another human being. There is also a sublimely heart-melting love story embedded in the midst of one of the most moving, relevant and attention-worthy plotlines I've had the pleasure of reading of late. Nothing about this book is cliché, been-done-before or mundane. This is an emotional roller-coaster that will take you out of your usual literary comfort zone, grip you and keep you at the edge of your seat, begging for more.<br /><br />Sophie Price is perfect. Her face is perfect. Her body is perfect. Everything in her life appears to be perfect. Her wealthy but neglectful parents have given her the type of lifestyle where everything has always been served to her on a silver platter, with no responsibilities or consequences for her actions. She is the 'Queen Bee' of her little click of entitled kids, wanting for nothing and taking it all unapologetically. She is selfish, self-centred, an awful friend who uses and discards people only to feed her starving ego. But when Sophie is alone, a scared and insecure little girl emerges at times, one that believes that her beautiful features hide only ugliness inside her. She detests that weakness in her, always striving not to show any real emotions in front of people, hoping no one would ever notice how meaningless her life really is.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I stood in front of the mirror and took a good hard look. I was as bare as I could make myself, no makeup with wet, stringy hair. I hated to look at myself in this state. I didn’t feel real. I felt too exposed and that made me exceedingly nervous, but I made myself look that morning. I memorized that girl. That girl was the real me. Frightened. Worthless. A terrible friend. Terrible daughter. Well educated but so limited in ideas worth having. Beautiful yet repulsive...”</i>
</blockquote><br />After indulging in a life of debauchery and vice, life finally catches up with Sophie, turning her entire existence upside down and throwing her in the midst of Africa to serve a six-month sentence at Masego, a struggling orphanage for children affected by war and violence. It is there that she meets Ian/Dingane, a young man who appears to only see the ‘ugly Sophie’ in her, one that does not belong or deserve to be at a place like Masego and one who would never make it there. For the first time in her privileged life, Sophie’s looks or possessions are not what define her. She is forced to dig deep inside her shallow soul for infinite amounts of courage, compassion and love for the sake of the innocents that fulfill her days with unconditional trust and affection. Through those children, Sophie learns to appreciate the gift of life, first and foremost, and to never again take what is given to her for granted.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“… what is there to be joyful about?”<br />“Life, Sophie. They still live. They breathe, they love each other, they find joy in the world around them for no other reason than because they are children. They are resilient. They will always rise above. Always. It is a curious facet of the innocent young.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Her relationship with Ian changes as well, their physical attraction continuously growing and the trust between them building a firm bond between them. Through Ian’s eyes, Sophie sees the person she wishes to become. He teaches her to draw strength from even the most painful of emotions, to see beauty in the small things in life and to love herself for her heart, not her appearance.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Fear, sadness. They’re not weaknesses. They are overpowering, defining emotions. They make you human, Sophie.”</i>
</blockquote><br />The connection between Ian and Sophie grows against all odds, two kindred spirits finding each other and desperately hanging onto one another in a dangerous world marred by political turmoil and instability, where survival and protection of those who cannot protect themselves becomes their first and only priority. Their love story develops gently and tastefully. Against a horrific backdrop of some of the worst sins that human nature is known to be responsible for, Sophie finally learns to love - love herself, love those who show her kindness, love those who deserve kindness from her. She also learns to love a man, deeply, openly and above all, selflessly.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Men wanted me. They all did, however briefly, but none of them wanted to keep me. That’s what I needed. I needed to be owned, loved. But not by a man. I knew then that I never needed to be kept by a man. What I needed was to love myself, to want to keep myself around. And in that revelation, I knew that if I wanted to keep myself, that a man wanting to keep me would just be a by-product. Who wouldn’t want to keep someone who respected himself or herself?”</i>
</blockquote><br />But this is not your average love story. Happiness has a hefty price tag in this beautiful tale of love, loss, courage and redemption. Our heroine travels a painful journey of self-discovery, learning to love and embrace the person she really is, and finally finding her true purpose in life. It is only then that Sophie truly becomes ‘beautiful’.<br /><br />A genuine work of art of new adult fiction, this story will stay with you, possess your every thought and make you feel. Everything.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“If we don’t make out of this alive, Sophie Price, I want you to know that I’ve never loved anyone as much as I love you. You’re it for me.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />~ N ♥<br /><br /><a href="http://wp.me/p2YIUs-15j" rel="nofollow noopener">See this review on my blog!</a> | <a href="http://www.facebook.com/natashaisabookjunkie" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow me on Facebook!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5305150356142571413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_619121086" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/619121086" />
    <a title="Claudia Ramírez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13061577-claudia-ram-rez"><img alt="Claudia Ramírez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533869692p2/13061577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/619121086?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claudia Ramírez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claudia Ramírez" href="/user/show/13061577-claudia-ram-rez">Claudia Ramírez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Nook 2940016131375" href="/book/show/16137702-vain">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13061577-claudia-ram-rez?shelf=expected-more">expected-more</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13061577-claudia-ram-rez?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer619121086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2003482274707208402">Three stars because I expected SO MUCH more. This book has so many good reviews and I was eager to read it, but it wasn't what I expected. Don't get me wrong, I liked it, but not as much. Sophie is a good main character and Ian is a prince, but I didn't fall in love with them. <br/><br/>All in all, is a good read, but oh, it took me more than a week to finish, which is strange in me because I usually don't take that long, I was so desperate to finish it! And I insist, is a good book, but I don't know, it </span>
  <span id="freeText2003482274707208402" style="display:none">Three stars because I expected SO MUCH more. This book has so many good reviews and I was eager to read it, but it wasn't what I expected. Don't get me wrong, I liked it, but not as much. Sophie is a good main character and Ian is a prince, but I didn't fall in love with them. <br /><br />All in all, is a good read, but oh, it took me more than a week to finish, which is strange in me because I usually don't take that long, I was so desperate to finish it! And I insist, is a good book, but I don't know, it lacked something.<br /><br />I just want to add that Spencer was my favorite character :).</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer505303473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13698858057568814591"><a href='http://www.freesmileys.org/smileys.php' title='Smiley' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380394708i/760021.gif' alt='Smiley' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><b>Sorry, I hate to go against the general consensus but I found this book very average.</b> <br/><br/>When I read the blup for this book I was really excited. <b>I couldn’t wait for this super hot Alpha bitch to shake up my world. Unfortunately she was crying by page 6 and I realised I had been conned! </b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Sophie Price</u>
</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1057.photobucket.com/user/poodding99/media/vain_zps5df53b17.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404987i/788474.jpg' alt=' photo vain_zps5df53b17.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>Now I realise that characters are supposed to have depth and dimension but <b>come on! </b> At least stick to your original synopsis for 1 chapter!<br/><br/>What this book is really about is Sophie, a beautif</span>
  <span id="freeText13698858057568814591" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.freesmileys.org/smileys.php" title="Smiley" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380394708i/760021.gif" alt="Smiley" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><b>Sorry, I hate to go against the general consensus but I found this book very average.</b> <br><br>When I read the blup for this book I was really excited. <b>I couldn’t wait for this super hot Alpha bitch to shake up my world. Unfortunately she was crying by page 6 and I realised I had been conned! </b><br><br><b>
  <u>Sophie Price</u>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1057.photobucket.com/user/poodding99/media/vain_zps5df53b17.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404987i/788474.jpg" alt=" photo vain_zps5df53b17.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Now I realise that characters are supposed to have depth and dimension but <b>come on! </b> At least stick to your original synopsis for 1 chapter!<br><br>What this book is really about is Sophie, a beautiful, spoiled but also painfully neglected socialite. That is sentenced to work in an orphanage in Africa after being arrested on drug charges.<br><br>Then comes the next thing that annoyed me. Almost instantly, from the moment Sophie get off the plane in Africa she transforms into a whole new person. I’m no expert but in my experience people evolve gradually they don’t become new people because they meet a hot guy and a happy airport worker!<br><a href="http://s1057.photobucket.com/user/poodding99/media/baobabsunset_zps4b63b20e.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404987i/788475.jpg" alt=" photo baobabsunset_zps4b63b20e.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>I live in Africa and while I have never been to Uganda I have traveled fairly extensively, and aside from a description of a baobab tree the author doesn't mention the scenery or animals once (except for bugs.)<b> It just seems strange to me to set a book in one of the most unique and beautiful environments in the world and then never really describe it!?</b> <br> <br><b>One thing I did like about this book was the portrayal of the orphanage and the children.</b><br><a href="http://s1057.photobucket.com/user/poodding99/media/children_zpsa6c2e919.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404987i/788476.jpg" alt=" photo children_zpsa6c2e919.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>I loved that despite their sad circumstances they were full of hope, excited to learn and always smiling.</b> Unfortunately I never really connected with any of the adult characters and I found the whole relationship between Sophie and Dingane rushed and a little disconnected. I also found this book predictable. <b>Also the more I think about it the more I find it a little insensitive that the author used such are real and horrific setting in such a superficial way.</b> The whole thing was just a set up for the romance!<br><br>And lastly and this is going to sound really cynical but <b>If hugging poor African orphans can miraculously fix vapid socialites then why hasn’t it worked on Paris Hilton?</b><br><a href="http://s1057.photobucket.com/user/poodding99/media/paris_hilton2180_zps234c0adc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404987i/788477.jpg" alt=" photo paris_hilton2180_zps234c0adc.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_457962050" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/457962050" />
    <a title="J" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10343430-j"><img alt="J" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/457962050?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J" href="/user/show/10343430-j">J</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Nook 2940016131375" href="/book/show/16137702-vain">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer457962050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5702252501270235583">WOW!<br/><br/><br/>This was NOT what I was expecting at all. <br/><br/>By 25% in I was unsure what was happening, I don't think I have ever read a character like Sophie... <br/><br/>Then <b>BAM!!</b> I was taken on an amazing journey. <br/><br/>Sophie Price is Vain. In every sense of the word. <br/><b>Vanity's a debilitating affliction. You're so absorbed in yourself it's impossible to love anyone other than oneself, leaving you weak without realisation of it. It's quite sad. You've no idea what you're missing either. You will never know real love and yo</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5702252501270235583" style="display:none">WOW!<br /><br /><br />This was NOT what I was expecting at all. <br /><br />By 25% in I was unsure what was happening, I don't think I have ever read a character like Sophie... <br /><br />Then <b>BAM!!</b> I was taken on an amazing journey. <br /><br />Sophie Price is Vain. In every sense of the word. <br /><b>Vanity's a debilitating affliction. You're so absorbed in yourself it's impossible to love anyone other than oneself, leaving you weak without realisation of it. It's quite sad. You've no idea what you're missing either. You will never know real love and your life will pass you by.</b><br /><br />Sophie is beautiful, rich, queen bee, wanted by all the guys, and all the girls want to be her friend because of it. <br />Her parents are so absorbed in themselves, Sophie has absolutely no restrictions, every want fulfilled and every desire quenched. <br /><br />Sophie is so broken and has no self respect I felt for her so much. <br /><br />Sophie is arrested for drug use and then sentenced 6 months to an Orphanage in Uganda. <br /><br />There we meet Ian. <br />Ahh Ian, I loved Ian. He calls Sophie out on being a spoilt brat from their 1st meeting. <br /><br /><b>"You won't last here. You'll stay blind to the environment that surrounds you. You'll live in your clean, perfect bubble and return to your posh life come six months. You are... you. I know your kind. I've seen it all before. You will never wake up. Not really,"</b> <br /><br />But the chemistry between Sophie and Ian gave me constant butterflies. <br /><b>It's my favourite part of my day."<br />My eyes opened lazily. "What do you mean?" I whispered.<br />"When you undo them and run your hand throughout the waves. That's my favourite part of my day."</b><br /><br />The two of them together were.. Amazing. I loved watching them interact and fall in love. They were believable and I loved experiencing that.<br /><b>"Your heart is startlingly beautiful, Sophie,"<br /><br />I'd been called beautiful so many times. It gratified me, validated me, but it was all empty, a facade. This was the first time someone had called me beautiful and it actually meant something to me. The praise slammed into my skin and permeated my body, leaving me flushed and overwhelmed.</b><br /><br />Sophie begins to change and its absolutely amazing to watch. <br /><b> A swelling sensation invaded my heart and I'd no idea what it was but it was a good hurt, a hurt that felt worthwhile.</b><br /><br /><b> I showed him I had enough initiative, enough industry, to strike out. I was also, simultaneously, recognising something in myself I didn't know could exist. <br />I was worth more than the sex I'd defined myself with.</b><br /><br />This was so much more than a love story, it takes you to orphans in Uganda and the Lord's Resistance Army. The subject isn't foreign to us, We know about it, we hear about what goes on and continue to be ignorant about it.<br /><br />I love books that take over and wrap you up in the world and the emotions of the characters, Fisher Amelie completely succeeded at this. It's Beautiful. It is horrifying.<br /><br /><b> No one can know sincere happiness, Sophie, without first having known sorrow. One can never appreciate the enormity and rareness of such a fiery bliss without seeing misery, however unfair that may be.</b><br /><br />Amazing 5 Shiny STARS! <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5702252501270235583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=e-pcs">e-pcs</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer499138178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2813533678208590221"><b>Fisher Amelie just posted that if VAIN gets 200 Amazon reviews by tonight (1-13-13), she will post a scene from Ian's POV. If you reviewed, this, please copy and paste your review on Amazon!!!!</b><br/><br/>My review:...4.5 Stars!!!!! <br/><br/><b>"There’s nothing redeeming about me. I’m a friend using, drug abusing, sex addict from Los Angeles. I’m every girlfriend’s worst nightmare and every boy’s fantasy."</b><br/><br/>And she fully admits it. Sophie Price is VAIN. Her identity comes from the clothes she wears, the money her parents</span>
  <span id="freeText2813533678208590221" style="display:none"><b>Fisher Amelie just posted that if VAIN gets 200 Amazon reviews by tonight (1-13-13), she will post a scene from Ian's POV. If you reviewed, this, please copy and paste your review on Amazon!!!!</b><br><br>My review:...4.5 Stars!!!!! <br><br><b>"There’s nothing redeeming about me. I’m a friend using, drug abusing, sex addict from Los Angeles. I’m every girlfriend’s worst nightmare and every boy’s fantasy."</b><br><br>And she fully admits it. Sophie Price is VAIN. Her identity comes from the clothes she wears, the money her parents give her, and who's boyfriend she can steal next. She's the leader of her elite group of friends and the <i>bow</i> to her. She's not just beautiful, she's physically perfect. She knows it, and they know it. <br><br> <span>[image error]</span><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404081i/786226._SY540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">"/&gt;<br><br>However, the term "Poor little rich girl" has never been so relevant. For although Sophie is surrounded by admirers, she is not adored, she is not loved, she isn't even wanted. If anything, her friends fear her rejection...and her parents don't care at all, <i>as long as Sophie keeps up appearances.</i> She sees herself as alone...a girl so hidden beneath her exterior that without the facade, she was nothing.<br><br>When Sophie's partying catches up with her for the second time, she is given an odd sentence, and one that finally makes her reveal some of her vulnerabilities. <br><br><b>"I stood in front of the mirror and took a good hard look. I was as bare as I could make myself, with no makeup, with wet, stringy hair. I hated to look at myself in this state. I didn't feel real I felt too exposed and that made me exceeding ly nerous, but I hamde myslef look that morning. I memorized that girl. <i>That girl was the real me. Frightened. Worthless. A terrible friend. Terrible daughter. Well educated but <u>so limited in ideas worth having. Beautiful yet repulsive...and finally honest.</u></i></b><br><br>She is to live and work in a Ugandan orphanage for six months. Six months without even the small luxuries like air conditioning, not to mention the round of immunizations that she undergoes, scares Sophie to death. But the trip is inevitable. She resigns herself to her future.<br><br>As soon as she gets off the plane, she realizes that her preconceptions are far from reality. The young man who is to pick her up and take her to her new home...Dingane...is the most handsome man she's ever seen. The first and only man to strike her speechless...and he <b>despises her.</b><br><br> <span>[image error]</span><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404081i/786227.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">"/&gt;<br><br>At first, Sophie is so awestruck, she can't even speak to him. And when she does, she sounds like an idiot...not at all the polished princess that she is back home in LA. So the two end up passing the trip to the orphanage in near silence. Dingane's disdain is palpable. When they finally reach her destination, Sophie realizes that nothing in the world could have prepared her for what she is greeted with. Nothing. Could EVER prepare her for the sight of the children and their stories. Most orphans get to be orphans because their parents die. <br><br><i>But rarely is the tragedy really an atrocity such as this.</i> And Sophie, the lucky American girl, will be forever changed, in such a fundamental, all encompassing way...that I soon forgot how she acted before. And so, it seems, does she.<br><br>We come to realize that the veneer of selfishness isn't the true Sophie, and that she is in fact a compassionate and loving person who was never given a chance. <br><br>One thing that I loved about the lessons that Sophie learned...she never, not once, tried to push the responsibility of her actions off on someone else. Even when she was scared, even when she was angry, even when she changed. She confronts her father, yes. But I admire not only her tenacity but her ability to take responsibility for the things she had done and truly want to change.<br><br>The family unit that makes up this orphanage is a mish mash of people all there for one reason...to give these poor children a place in life, to make them fell loved and to give them as much happiness as possible in a world that has forgotten they exist. <br><br><b>"How many are there?" I asked.<br>"Fifty nine." She said succinctly. "We're only equipped to handle twenty."<br>"How do you manage?" I asked quietly, taking in the expanse of children.<br>"We just do. Lots of faith, my love. It always works out in the end. Somehow. Somehow we turn thirty beds into sixty. Somehow we stretch our food to impossible measures. Somehow we survive on our impossible meager income. Somehow we love them all equally. Somehow."</b> <br><br>It's a wonderful journey for this young woman. It's a fairly quick realizations that she has that this is the happiest she's been in quite some time. And amid the tragedy that is all around them, every day, these children and their caretakers have a full life.<br><br><b>"Why do they do it?"<br>"Because it brings them joy."<br>"And what is there to be joyful about?" I asked honestly....<br>"Life, Sophie. They still live. They breathe, they love each other, they find joy in the world around them for no other reason than because they are children. They are resilient. They will always rise above. Always. It is a curious facet of the innocent young..."</b><br><br> <span>[image error]</span><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404081i/786228.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">"/&gt;<br><br>Somehow, Sophie and Dingane, or Ian as some call him, find time to steal covert looks and longing glances behind each others backs. And a friendship is born. An affection built on respect for one another and admiration. And, of course, simple, frustrating LUST.<br><br><b>"How could someone bug the shit out of you so much and yet simultaneously cause you to want to know them intimately with your tongue? He was driving me crazy....As soon as my head hit the pillow, I dreamt of Dingane's ridiculous hands"</b><br><br>While I loved, loved the story, I can't give it all stars because there were quite a few noticeable editing errors...misspelled words, misplaced words, punctuations mistakes. Those weren't too bad, honestly, but there were also inconsistencies in execution and things that didn't make sense. Not often, but enough to give the flow a little hiccup.<br><br>Still, this story moved me, in a way that few can. I imagine that it will move anyone who reads it...the subject matter and execution, the events that unfold after Sophie gets to Africa are images that will stick with you. They simultaneously break your heart and mend the pieces. I cried, cried, CRIED!!!!! And yet this still has a beautiful message, and an uplifting one. I imagine that things work out for Sophie and her crew much easier than they do in real life, but this is fiction.<br><br>If this book has a question mark beside it, I encourage you to give it a try. Although I must admit, I was a bit bored when Sophie was spending her time bragging about how beautiful she is, after getting to Uganda, the story does a complete 180 and I was captivated. Beautifully done, Ms. Amelie. What a great way to get the message out and still tell an amazing love story!<br><br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2813533678208590221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText9756337521797963026" style="display:none">I'm not sure what happened. I read <i>Vain</i> 2 or 3 weeks ago (don't even remember now) and UHHHHH...didn't review the thing?<br /><br />I'm sure that I have quotes marked in my copy, but the distance of time has me super lazy to care enough to go pull them up.<br /><br /><b>Condensed Review Version</b> : <br /><br /><i>The cons -</i><br /><br />Simplistic writing<br />Some minimal editing issues<br />Cringe-worthy start (almost DNF'ed) for the first few chapters (but I get the point the author was trying to make, so it's forgivable)<br />A character who unbelievably changed overnight (would have liked to have seen a slower change) from spoiled rich brat to empathetic, hard working, mature woman<br /><br /><i>The pros -</i><br /><br />Very readable<br />Tugs at the heartstrings<br />AWESOME, strong, HUMBLE, caring, male lead<br />Attention brought to a part of the world that westerners could stand to learn more about<br /><br />The second half of this book was a powerhouse of emotion. Seeing a materialistic girl become a person who cared about orphans whose lives were ravaged by war and genocide took the typical YA/NA contemporary standard and threw it out the window. <br /><br />While not perfect in execution, this story got the focus off of generic teen problems and took the reader to another place entirely. Even with the hiccups, I have to credit an A for effort. <br /></span>

<div id="review_499088519" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/499088519" />
    <a title="destini mia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13742215-destini-mia"><img alt="destini mia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499903277p2/13742215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/499088519?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destini mia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destini mia" href="/user/show/13742215-destini-mia">destini mia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Nook 2940016131375" href="/book/show/16137702-vain">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13742215-destini-mia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer499088519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16237055965069713497"><b>This is by far one of the my favorite reads of 2013.</b> <br/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/495359.gif' width='400' height='250' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>Sophie Price is... vain (hence the title). She has no care in the world, except for what she wants, and does anything and everything to get there. She has used every single person she has surrounded herself with and only has one true friend. She spends her days being the dutiful daughter and her weekends partying and doing drugs. <br/>When she gets caught doing drugs a second time, she's sentenced to six months in Africa to volunteer at an orphanag</span>
  <span id="freeText16237055965069713497" style="display:none"><b>This is by far one of the my favorite reads of 2013.</b> <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/495359.gif" width="400" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Sophie Price is... vain (hence the title). She has no care in the world, except for what she wants, and does anything and everything to get there. She has used every single person she has surrounded herself with and only has one true friend. She spends her days being the dutiful daughter and her weekends partying and doing drugs. <br>When she gets caught doing drugs a second time, she's sentenced to six months in Africa to volunteer at an orphanage. <br><br><br>I <b>loved</b> how different the book started out. Even the blurb was unique. We didn't get the "I'm so vain and only care about myself, but the instant I met him and the heavens shined down on me and I became the selfless person I always knew I could be." She was selfish and she knew it. The world revolved around her. <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380404074ra/786215.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><i>I abandoned myself to every whim I felt. Every want I fulfilled and every desire was quenched. I wanted for nothing.</i><br><br><br>Things start to change when she goes to Africa. She meets Dingane/Ian and they have an... interesting first meeting. She was so accustomed to guys tripping over themselves for her, that when her didn't, it took her off guard. The orphanage was something that also took her off guard. Amelie Fisher doesn't hesitate to show you the really frightening and painful side. <br><br><br>Ian "Dingane" Aberdeen was incredible. I loved that he played the whole "I really don't like you" card, but still did really sweet things (like with the bugs). He was so sexy and confident, but at the same time he was... cute? Innocent? I really can't find the right word. We also learn about his life and it was amazing to see how well he could relate to Sophie. <br><br><br>This is a love story, so they do fall in love but it wasn't easy getting there. There were beautiful moments, sad moments, and there were laugh-out-loud moments and I loved reading every word. <br><br><br><i>"I was not staring at you," he told his plate.<br>I leaned over. "Did you hear that, Dingane's lunch? He was not staring at you."<br>He looked up at me crossly. "I was not staring at <b>you</b>."<br>"I never said you were."<br>"I was merely explaining that Henry was exaggerating. I did not stare at you."<br>"Okay," I stated, implying in my tone that he was doing just that.<br>"I didn't. I-I wasn't"<br>"I believe you," I told him.<br>"I may have looked at you a few times to make sure you were doing your job."<br>"Oh, I see then."<br>"But I certainly wasn't <b>staring</b>."<br>"We've established that you were not staring."<br>He breathed deeply a few times, his eyes burning into mine. "Good."<br>He'd definitely been staring. </i><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380404074ra/786216.gif" width="400" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Little by little he slowly brought down her shields. He helped her open up and break that wall she always kept around her heart.<br><br><br><i>
  <b>"Fear, sadness. They're not weaknesses. They are overpowering, defining emotions. They make you human, Sophie."</b>
</i><br><br><br>The orphanage plays a big part in the story and it was <b>heart breaking</b>. These kids found hope where there wasn't much to me found. They laughed, sang, and played in the water. There living conditions made me cringe and yet, they found reasons to smile.<br><br><br><i>
  <b>"And what is there to be joyful about? <br>"Life, Sophie. They still live. They breathe, they love each other, they find joy in the world around them for no other reason than because they are children. They are resilient. They will always rise above. Always."</b>
</i><br><br><br>There was a short but incredibly sweet ending that brought a huge smile to my face. <br><br><br><i>
  <b>"The shortest distance between two points is the line from me to you."</b>
</i><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380335959ra/694575.gif" width="400" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16237055965069713497" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
